<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_191394789">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/191394789" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3015503-maria-grazia" class="left imgcol" title="Maria Grazia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347724212p2/3015503.jpg" alt="Maria Grazia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/191394789?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 31, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3015503-maria-grazia" class="user" title="Maria Grazia">Maria Grazia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades" title="Paperback 9780099465829" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3015503-maria-grazia?shelf=read-in-2011" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer191394789">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6555353612075482239"><em>“Set in the Georgian period, about 20 years before the Regency, These Old Shades is considered to be the book that launched Heyer’s career. It features two of Heyer’s most memorable characters: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon, and Leonie, whom he rescues from a life of ignomy and comes to love and marry”</em>.<br /><strong>My review </strong><br />If you meet Satanas in a dark alley in the middle of the night and you are desperately seeking escape from a wretched life of violence and harassment, maybe you’d be as happy as youn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6555353612075482239"><em>“Set in the Georgian period, about 20 years before the Regency, These Old Shades is considered to be the book that launched Heyer’s career. It features two of Heyer’s most memorable characters: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon, and Leonie, whom he rescues from a life of ignomy and comes to love and marry”</em>.<br /><strong>My review </strong><br />If you meet Satanas in a dark alley in the middle of the night and you are desperately seeking escape from a wretched life of violence and harassment, maybe you’d be as happy as young Leòn at becoming his, body and soul, bought for a diamond pin. Very happy to become his page and wear good clothes, to follow him wherever his libertine life led him without complaining, without questioning. <br />Especially if Satanas is just a nickname for a rich, elegant, fascinating nobleman: Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon. And mainly if he appears to you like this:<br /><em>“ He walked mincingly, for the red heels of his shoes were very high. A long purple cloak, rose-lined, hung from his shoulders and was allowed to fall carelessly back from his dress, revealing a full-skirted coat of purple satin, heavily laced with gold; a waistcoat of flowered silk; faultless small clothes; and a lavish sprinkling of jewels on his cravat and breast”</em>.<br />Leòn’s new life as Avon’s page will lead the youth from a murky Parisian backstreet to the corrupt splendours of 18th century Versailles and the dignified mansions of England. If you were the young boy saved by the illustrious man from a horrible life of ill-treatmments, wouldn’t you admire him immensely, though everybody else considers him selfish, arrogant and even cruel? <br />This is precisely what Leòn starts doing. The child’s worshipping admiration for the Duke - Monseigneur, as he calls him – becomes amusement to the libertine’s old friends and, strangely enough, a menace to his old enemy, the Comte de Saint-Vire. In fact, the reason why the Duke bought Leòn was that he was struck by the boy's unusual colouring, which reminds him of his enemy's red hair and dark brows. <br />When Leòn is revealed to be Leonie , the story gets even more intriguing with the Duke making her his ward to be introduced at Versailles … (read this brilliant page online)<br />This is the beginning of an incredible series of enticing fast-paced adventures mingling intrigue, romance and the unmistakable Heyer mark, her incredible wit. A real romp to read all in one go to the very end.<br />What is incredible is that we have these incredible gripping characters taking shape under our eyes through their delightful dialogue exchanges and the incredible pressing flow of actions; all of them, even the secondary ones (i.e. Mr. Manvers, the Curé or Madame de Saint-Vire) are very neatly connoted , though only with a few thorough brushstrokes.<br />The two protagonists are outstanding and peculiar, though they have the trademark Heyer clearly printed on themselves. Justin Alastair is …<em>” known by the soubriquet Satanas, for his cold exactitude and prescient understanding of what his opponent will do next, as well as a certain elasticity in his moral fiber. The Duke has restored his family’s fortune through gambling; he is, as one would expect of one of the first peers of the realm, an arrant snob, careful, although certainly flamboyant, in his dress, and punctilious in manner” </em>(from Vic Sanborn’s review at Jane Austen’s World). <br />Someone told me Leonie is possibly Heyer’s least admired heroine. This sounds so impossible to me! However , I read that she is one of the characters Heyers herself loved most and I myself loved her immensely. Leonie is as loveable as flawed, a whirling personality, an oddly naïve female rogue, an irresistibly charming - though very little accomplished - young lady, ravishing beautiful and disarmingly stubborn, brave and fragile at the same time. If she can wrap the formidable Duke of Avon around her little finger with a smile and a gaze full of admiration under her lashes, how can we resist her ?<br />The plot is very well designed but readers need a great fix of … suspension of disbelief, of course. As for me, I’ve gone through the story with a constant smile on my face and making a great effort to put it down from time to time.<br /><strong>These Old Shades</strong> is the first book in the Alastairs Trilogy and I’m glad about it . This means there is more delight expecting me and many other willing readers out there, in <strong>Devil’s Cub</strong> and in <strong>An Infamous Army</strong>.<br />My review is on my blog too, FLY HIGH, at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://bit.ly/oDl2vT" target="_blank">http://bit.ly/oDl2vT</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6555353612075482239">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer38078358">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16082781364802649403">I enjoyed this, despite one or two minor annoyances:<br /><br />1. The hero was referred to by any one of about eleven different names or titles randomly throughout - "Justin" "The Duke" "Alastair" "Avon" "His Grace". PICK ONE AND STICK WITH IT, HEYER.<br />2. Leonie was funny but a bit of a twerp, she definitely didn't act 19 and her worshipful ADORATION of Alistavonjustingraceduke got on my nerves, as did his condescending "come here and let me wipe my feet on you, my infant" attitude to her. <br />3. What reference</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16082781364802649403">I enjoyed this, despite one or two minor annoyances:<br /><br />1. The hero was referred to by any one of about eleven different names or titles randomly throughout - "Justin" "The Duke" "Alastair" "Avon" "His Grace". PICK ONE AND STICK WITH IT, HEYER.<br />2. Leonie was funny but a bit of a twerp, she definitely didn't act 19 and her worshipful ADORATION of Alistavonjustingraceduke got on my nerves, as did his condescending "come here and let me wipe my feet on you, my infant" attitude to her. <br />3. What reference does the title 'these old shades' have to anything in the book?<br />4. Low-born people are dull, stodgy, unattractive and into farming - they're just BORN with an inbuilt longing to get out there with a plough and start turning over some arable land. Nobility are noticably beautiful and delicate, and also far more intelligent. <br />5. I didn't really feel the romance from Leonie's angle. When did she stop seeing him as a father figure and start seeing him as a romantic figure? Or did she love him in a strictly non-platonic way from the start? We never really got inside her head. <br /><br />The age difference didn't bother me at all, I think it's fine as long as they're both happy. Put it this way: Johnny Depp, Patrick Dempsey, Gerard Butler and Viggo Mortensen are all in their 40s, and still attractive to someone 20 years younger (ie me).</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_118232381">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118232381" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" title="Wealhtheow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" alt="Wealhtheow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/118232381?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 25, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="user" title="Wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/3405157-these-old-shades" title="Paperback 9780373773404" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer118232381">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1519177978475752164">Justin Alistair is handsome, fashionable, and merciless. As the Duke of Avon in the mid-Eighteenth century, he has far more power and money than he really knows what to do with. An urchin's red hair catches his attention, and he buys the boy from his loutish older brother. <br /><br />And thus begins the adventure of Leon, also known as Leonie, and her life with the duke. She has a sort of slavish devotion to him that is utterly inexplicable (and quite disturbs his friends), and he intends to use her to des</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1519177978475752164">Justin Alistair is handsome, fashionable, and merciless. As the Duke of Avon in the mid-Eighteenth century, he has far more power and money than he really knows what to do with. An urchin's red hair catches his attention, and he buys the boy from his loutish older brother. <br /><br />And thus begins the adventure of Leon, also known as Leonie, and her life with the duke. She has a sort of slavish devotion to him that is utterly inexplicable (and quite disturbs his friends), and he intends to use her to destroy his enemy, Saint-Vire. First she acts as his page, and when that masquerade wears thin, he commences a sort of My Fair Lady makeover and presents her to Society. <br /><br />In most ways, <a title="These Old Shades by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades">These Old Shades</a> falls into the usual Heyer tropes: the hero is saturnine, sarcastic, the best at everything, and has a hilariously unlikely nickname ("Satanas"); the heroine is the most sensible and cheerful girl ever, is the only one who thinks the hero has a heart-of-gold, acts younger than her years (Leonie acts so young, in fact, that she often seems closer to ten than her purported age of nineteen) and is absolutely beautiful; everyone is fascinated by the two love interests. <br /><br />The relationship between Justin and Leonie will always be a bit creepy: he's more than twice her age, he *bought* her, and he has very different moral standards for men than for women. Leonie herself is actually pretty charming, although I don't buy her characterization for a moment--there's no way someone can work on a farm and then a tavern for ~20 years and be so innocent and flaky. And I just don't understand why she's so devoted to him, nor do I understand when she turned from thinking of him as a protector to a lover. She makes comments about how men her age are too silly and foolish--but she's at least as silly as they are. But here is the saving grace of this book: there are other characters beyond Justin and Leonie. Not just the usual collection of silly women and amusing children, who serve to make the love interests look better, but married couples whose relationships to each other are delicately traced, a young rake who doesn't understand why his older brother has turned his biting wit against him, and the kindly Davenant, who is a gentle scholarly presence in the background. Their tangled interactions with each other kept me amused by the book long after I tired of the foregone love between Leonie and Justin. I hate the mid-eighteenth century, but there is one thing to be said for it--by setting her story there, Heyer is unable to lard her dialog with Regency slang. What a relief! As always with Heyer, there's a huge dose of classism in here--in fact, it's necessary to believe that peasants are cloddish and yearn for the earth, and nobles are delicate and intelligent, in order for the plot to make sense.<br /><br />(I really disliked the plot of this book. Justin reaches a scandalous conclusion based on very threadbare evidence, then spends the entire book acting as though he is absolutely positive that it's true. It's only sheer luck that he's correct, and the easier and more probable solution to why Leonie resembles Saint-Vire is wrong. It just all felt frustratingly unlikely.)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1519177978475752164">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer525267049">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11344699629976197005">I absolutely loved this book so much. Even two years later, just thinking of the book gives me a warm feeling from inside. It was such a darling book, with the hero being such a cynical, jaded character, and Leonie, our heroine, being a breath of fresh air to him, sweet and innocent and loving and trusting. I have never read a book as sweet, or as filled with bittersweet angst, as this one. <br /><br />And it was also my first Heyer book, one that got me hooked onto Heyer and turned me into an eternal fan.<br /><br />T</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11344699629976197005">I absolutely loved this book so much. Even two years later, just thinking of the book gives me a warm feeling from inside. It was such a darling book, with the hero being such a cynical, jaded character, and Leonie, our heroine, being a breath of fresh air to him, sweet and innocent and loving and trusting. I have never read a book as sweet, or as filled with bittersweet angst, as this one. <br /><br />And it was also my first Heyer book, one that got me hooked onto Heyer and turned me into an eternal fan.<br /><br />This book is one of my ideals as to what a romance novel should be ??</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1214803890">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1214803890" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/25867535-carol---georgia-font-on-my-mind" class="left imgcol" title="Carol - Georgia font on my mind!"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451531333p2/25867535.jpg" alt="Carol - Georgia font on my mind!" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1214803890?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25867535-carol---georgia-font-on-my-mind" class="user" title="Carol - Georgia font on my mind!">Carol - Georgia font on my mind!</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades" title="Paperback 9780099465829" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/25867535-carol---georgia-font-on-my-mind?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25867535-carol---georgia-font-on-my-mind?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1214803890">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13609021750637126320">Group Read Georgette Heyer Group<br /><br />This was my favourite book as a very young teen &amp; I have read it more than any other title!<br /><br />GH was not altogether happy with The Black Moth &amp; decided to bring back Devil Belmanoir - this time as the romantic hero. This is well known, but also Lavinia &amp; Richard become Fanny &amp; Edward, Frank Fortescue becomes Hugh Davenant, Diana becomes Lady Merivale. I don't think Lord Merivale is Jack - he lacks Jack's whimsical sweetness. But their &amp; Belmanoir'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13609021750637126320">Group Read Georgette Heyer Group<br /><br />This was my favourite book as a very young teen &amp; I have read it more than any other title!<br /><br />GH was not altogether happy with The Black Moth &amp; decided to bring back Devil Belmanoir - this time as the romantic hero. This is well known, but also Lavinia &amp; Richard become Fanny &amp; Edward, Frank Fortescue becomes Hugh Davenant, Diana becomes Lady Merivale. I don't think Lord Merivale is Jack - he lacks Jack's whimsical sweetness. But their &amp; Belmanoir's back story is used to very good effect.<br /><br />The extract from a poem by Victorian poet Austin Dobson (which has been at the front of every edition I have read of this novel except the Arrow)<br /><br /><em> This Age I grant (and grant with pride),<br />Is varied, rich, eventful;<br />But, if you touch its weaker side,<br />Deplorably resentful:<br /><br />Belaud it, and it takes your praise<br />With air of calm conviction;<br />Condemn it, and at once you raise<br />A storm of contradiction.<br /><br />Whereas with these old Shades of mine,<br />Their ways and dress delight me;<br />And should I trip by word or line,<br />They cannot well indict me. </em><br /><br />This story is so well told that I simply don't care about major plot holes. I don't care that Avon treating 19 year old Leonie like a child &amp; withholding information from her that she had a right to know. I don't care that French characters in this book who are fluent in English fall back into their French for very easy English terms. What I do care about is the Romance with a capital R that sweeps you along &amp; makes this book nearly impossible to put down. Yes it is flawed but GH was still only around 23 when she wrote it - this is an accomplished book for <em>anyone</em> let alone so young an author!<br /><br /><em>&amp;</em> I do love is the way that GH manages to make the dress of the time look masculine - no easy task. I love the rich cast of characters that, like a few of her other great works, become a group of friends that you want to hang out with. &amp; Rupert &amp; Leonie's relationship is quite complex. She is more than a sister to them - yet they are not in love.<br /><br />&amp; the book does contain some of the greatest lines in romantic fiction.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<em>“Léonie, you will do well to consider. You are not the first woman in my life."<br /><br />She smiled through her tears. "Monseigneur, I would so much rather be the last woman than the first,” she said.” <br /><br /></em>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />What can one do but *swoon*<br /><br />Can't wait to read the sequel Devil's Club next month.<br /><br /><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13609021750637126320">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_860601311">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/860601311" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1901531-abra" class="left imgcol" title="Abra"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1251241273p2/1901531.jpg" alt="Abra" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/860601311?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1901531-abra" class="user" title="Abra">Abra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades" title="Paperback 9780099465829" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1901531-abra?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1901531-abra?shelf=history" class="actionLinkLite">history</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1901531-abra?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer860601311">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6588159225049988069">This is the first Georgette Heyer book I've read and I'm astonished. Astonished I had never read her before and astonished I liked it so much! Honestly, I wasn't anticipating much... I knew she was the "creator of regency romance" but I kind of figured the genre must have improved since 1926.<br /><br />Nope.<br /><br />In fact, I realized that I have over the years read multiple blatant rip-offs of this exact novel (right down to the scene where Leonie and Fanny are arguing about pants) and none of them even come clos</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6588159225049988069">This is the first Georgette Heyer book I've read and I'm astonished. Astonished I had never read her before and astonished I liked it so much! Honestly, I wasn't anticipating much... I knew she was the "creator of regency romance" but I kind of figured the genre must have improved since 1926.<br /><br />Nope.<br /><br />In fact, I realized that I have over the years read multiple blatant rip-offs of this exact novel (right down to the scene where Leonie and Fanny are arguing about pants) and none of them even come close to touching on the original!<br /><br />Heyer doesn't appear to be everyones cup of tea, of course. Arguable flaws of the novel are that it is extremely dialogue heavy (the conversations can become tedious) and it uses historically accurate fashions (one has to be okay with their sexy heroes wearing powdered wigs and high heels and more jewelry than a Kardashian.) Descriptive prose seems a little scattershot, too.<br /><br />But the good far outweighs the bad!<br /><br />I expected a book like this to lag but it was surprisingly well paced. It is very witty. The characters were all very loveable. Leonie is probably one of the best romance heroines I've ever read. I would totally want to be buddies with her. The romance between Avon and Leonie was remarkably cool, in that it didn't unfold in the traditional way, and it made you think. (The age difference didn't bother me, the hero worship made me wonder, but in the end it was perfect.) It was refreshing to read a romance that had no heaving bosoms and quivering loins, by the way. It made small gestures, like the way Leonie would kiss Avon's wrist, far more powerful.<br /><br />I was surprised how damned FUNNY this novel was. A lot of scenes made me chuckle. Leonie was hilarious with her ranting and her gleeful blood thirst and her "bah!" Rupert was a hoot. Avon was priceless. I loved how he waltzed around with that fan he knew damn well everyone hated, and how he pretended to forget everything, and how prudish he was about Leonie's colorful language. He was a character with a lot of depth, somehow managing to be both kind and cruel, both foppish and masculine.<br /><br />Incidentally, (and this is a love-it or hate-it) the story was never told from a particular point of view. It followed Avon through most of it, occasionally detouring to Leonie, but you really never knew what either of them were thinking or feeling. You had to infer it from their actions just like everyone else in the book. I liked that. Some might not.<br /><br />I will definitely be reading more Heyer.<br /><br />Never did figure out what the title means...</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6588159225049988069">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17060652112415463393">Bah, as Leonie would say. I wrote a review and it didn't get saved for some reason. <br /><br />Anyway, my reaction to this book can be summed up in one word: CREEPY! Here's why:<br /><br />1. Avon <em>buys</em> Leon/Leonie from her brother. Ew. <br />2. The age difference between Avon and Leonie (20+ years) was a bit much for me. A Heyer hero is often several years older than the heroine, but 20+ years put Avon into the creepy old man category for me.<br />3. Avon calls Leonie "my infant" half the time, which just reinforced #2 for me. UGH. I realize this could be meant as the French <em>mon enfant</em>, but that didn't make it any easier for me to deal with.<br />4. Avon was just a little too foppish for me. I like a well dressed hero, but a fan? Yes, the book is set earlier than Heyer's Regency novels, so men's clothes were more elaborate in general, but still.<br />5. Leonie's hand kissing and "master"-ing and general subservience grated on me. I know she was his page, but it was a bit much. <br /><br />My favorite part was Avon's retelling of Leonie's story in front of her real parents. Very tense and fun to read. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5678722742636949633">This was a great story. I didn't even miss the sex. Despite being written years ago, it didn't feel the least bit dated. <br /><br />Loved the hero with his bad self and his little "quizzing glass."   <span style="display:none" id="freeText5678722742636949633">This was a great story. I didn't even miss the sex. Despite being written years ago, it didn't feel the least bit dated. <br /><br />Loved the hero with his bad self and his little "quizzing glass." The heroine was free and sassy, even as a servant, but I thought she could be a little air-headed at times and definitely bloodthirsty. I guess that would be a good match for a hero who was suppose to be the devil...and for someone who spent 7 years as a boy. <br /><br />Some events at the end took me by surprise. (That certainly weren't dated.) Didn't think the bad guy's crime fit his punishment. Maybe I'm wrong. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the detail. Between the powdered wigs and the satiny pink and purple clothes and red high heels with diamond buckles (worn by the men, no less), I would've been weirded out. <br /><br />This is one that will stick with me awhile. <span id="freeTextContainer13666233946805510279">The plot was a cliche when Heyer wrote it as a young woman (basically Cinderella, underscoring that "blood will always tell") but Heyer writes it with such wit and dash that it never really stales. I think her Georgians are slightly better than the Regency tales, with an exception or two--they are tighter paced, and the world of the mid-1700s is beautifully evoked; it was obvious in later years that Heyer had read Chesterfield's letters when she created Avon.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer135705278">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15915462328551866494">My second Georgette Heyer! I read this trilogy out of order and read Devils Cub first but it was so fun to go back and see how his parents got together! <br /><br />This book has the whole girl dressed as a boy trope but with a twist and whole lot of intrigue and conspiracy behind how the heroine came to need that disguise. All is not fully revealed until the end of the book and the slow revelation of her history was very well done. <br /><br />As far as the romance goes, I had a hard time with it in the beginning. The</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15915462328551866494">My second Georgette Heyer! I read this trilogy out of order and read Devils Cub first but it was so fun to go back and see how his parents got together! <br /><br />This book has the whole girl dressed as a boy trope but with a twist and whole lot of intrigue and conspiracy behind how the heroine came to need that disguise. All is not fully revealed until the end of the book and the slow revelation of her history was very well done. <br /><br />As far as the romance goes, I had a hard time with it in the beginning. The hero is 20 years older than the heroine and continually calls her 'infant' and 'my child' and at one point tells someone that he 'thinks of her as a granddaughter'. So initially this was pretty high on ick factor for me and I didn't know if I could get over it. Now I'm not sure exactly at what point this changed for me but by the time time the hero pronounces his love for her and they kiss at the end I was cheering and sighing over the sweetness of it all. This is the talent of this author! Somehow slowly over the course of the story their relationship grew and developed and the ick factor disappeared for me. Not sure exactly how or when, just slowly over the story it started to work for me. <br /><br />Overall this book was just great. I adored the heroine and all of the characters really. The romance was solid, the story was paced well, I laughed out loud more than once, it was just great! Highly recommended!</span>

      <a href="/user/show/2986995-mary-ronan-drew" class="user" title="Mary Ronan Drew">Mary Ronan Drew</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6807878-these-old-shades" title="Paperback 9781402219474" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1464530196'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1464530196">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12467417223966662505">An early Georgette Heyer novel that has everything: a revenge plot, a rags to riches story, a reformed rake, the growth of a girl into a woman, regret, confession, reconciliation, love, and a happy ending.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer3235008540789536154">I have hesitated to add a review of this because I'm pretty sure I can't do it justice. Brilliantly written, witty, fun and spot on historically. The Duke of Avon is one of the best heroes ever written. I love him and I can't see that anyone other than Leonie could have broken through his shell. Even though the romance is not torrid, you can see that absolute love he has for her. Sigh...</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_934349725">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/934349725" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2733854-tanja" class="left imgcol" title="Tanja"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1376687513p2/2733854.jpg" alt="Tanja" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/934349725?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 16, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2733854-tanja" class="user" title="Tanja">Tanja</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6807878-these-old-shades" title="Paperback 9781402219474" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=historical-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=read-in-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2014</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2733854-tanja?shelf=awesome" class="actionLinkLite">awesome</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer934349725">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6124576560156265677">Oh, wow, this has got to be one of my favorite books. I loved every minute of reading this. I like sarcasm and the main character, Duke of Avon, is the most sarcastic character I ever read about. He’s about 40 years old and he’s quite notorious. He doesn't seem that bad to me, but the book takes place in 18th century, when I suppose people were more easily shocked.<br /><br />Avon’s life changes when he comes across Leon, a 19 year old boy who later turns out to be a girl, Leonie. She sees Avon as her savio</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6124576560156265677">Oh, wow, this has got to be one of my favorite books. I loved every minute of reading this. I like sarcasm and the main character, Duke of Avon, is the most sarcastic character I ever read about. He’s about 40 years old and he’s quite notorious. He doesn't seem that bad to me, but the book takes place in 18th century, when I suppose people were more easily shocked.<br /><br />Avon’s life changes when he comes across Leon, a 19 year old boy who later turns out to be a girl, Leonie. She sees Avon as her savior and the best person in the world. She sticks with that opinion regardless of how many people tell her that she’s wrong. Leonie has had a hard life and she can be both innocent and wise. She’s not afraid of Avon and the way she talks to him surprises people around them.<br /><br />Usually when I’m reading a book, there is at least one character that I think is boring and needs to disappear, but this time, I thought everyone was interesting. I wish there were more conversations between Hugh and Justin, and more details on how they became friends. And I’d like to know exactly what happened between Justin and Jennifer. The mystery of Leonie's parents was too easily solved (“Oh, that guy wants to have a farm? He’s probably adopted.”) and seriously, how did Avon know that Leonie is a girl?<br /><br />As much as I like the book, I have to say that their relationship isn’t exactly normal. He’s twice her age, he calls her ‘my infant’ and she really worships him. He sometimes seems older than he is and she frequently seems younger than she is. He’s like a father figure to her, which makes their romantic relationship even weirder. I still can’t help but absolutely love the story. It’s not the first time a book made me like something I probably shouldn't.<br /><br />The book takes place in England and France. The characters sometimes use french words. I liked that, because I’m currently learning French and every bit of practice helps.<br /><br />This is the first book by Georgette Heyer that I've read and I hope all of her books are as well written as this one. The style is so elegant and witty, it’s wonderful to read. I was crazy excited while reading this. One thing I don’t understand – why is there no movie adaptation? It would be so great to watch this.</span>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_818954141">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/818954141" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19799133-maria" class="left imgcol" title="Maria"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1382981396p2/19799133.jpg" alt="Maria" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/818954141?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 12, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19799133-maria" class="user" title="Maria">Maria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6807878-these-old-shades" title="Paperback 9781402219474" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19799133-maria?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer818954141">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer322855243040757410">One night, on his way back home, Justin Alastair, His Grace the Duke of Avon, stumbles across Léon, a poor boy who is running away from his bad brother. To save him, the Duke decides to buy him and to make him his page. But His Grace never does anything on a simple whim, he has a precise purpose which drove him to act like that. What does the Duke of Avon want from a stranger little boy who loves and worships his saviour? Things get more complicated and mysterious when Léon is forced to reveal t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText322855243040757410">One night, on his way back home, Justin Alastair, His Grace the Duke of Avon, stumbles across Léon, a poor boy who is running away from his bad brother. To save him, the Duke decides to buy him and to make him his page. But His Grace never does anything on a simple whim, he has a precise purpose which drove him to act like that. What does the Duke of Avon want from a stranger little boy who loves and worships his saviour? Things get more complicated and mysterious when Léon is forced to reveal the truth about himself... she is actually a girl, named Léonie. <br /><br />I think Georgette Heyer’s novels are the funniest books I have ever read! I always enjoy reading them, both her Georgian stories and her Regency ones. There is always a humorous aspect which makes me smile but also reflect on the characters’ personality and their manners. Every Heyer character has a strong nature and you cannot help but sympathise with them, even the devilish ones. Some people might call that sympathy for the devil and I suppose it is true.<br /><br />I would never have imagined to feel anything different from disdain about a man like Justin Alastair, the Duke of Avon, and yet I think very highly of him! He is a man in his forties, with a very bad past. He had many women and loved perhaps only one and he always got what he wanted, without a care in the world. He has lots of enemies and he is dreaded anywhere. You simply need to know his moniker is Satanas! Now, would you ever think you could possibly love him? Or even like him? I would not. But I did like him and I did love him! And I am sure whoever read this novel will do that. The reason is simple. I believe people who love him, do that because of his behaviour towards Léonie, all the bad things he has done disappear thanks to his generosity and affection for this apparently poor girl. When his brother, Lord Rupert, describes him as “cunning, devilish cunning” gives us a perfect description of his nature but, like all the greatest heroes, he has a heart... deep down. And I can assure you would like to get to know him better. I did! The best thing, which I believe is the basis of this story, is to witness the change in Avon’s nature. There is a scene where he seems another man, he is scared, hopeless and he is ready to give up anything for the woman he loves and that (at least in my opinion) is the point of the novel. Can a devilish man redeem himself for love? I definitely cannot answer this question! You will find it out if you read “These old shades”.<br /><br />Léonie, the heroine, is a childish creature, she is nineteen when Avon saves her but she seems a little girl throughout the entire novel. Fortunately, she shows another trait of herself by the end of the book and I liked that, because she finally forgets her masculine side. Nevertheless, she is brave and determined enough to make the cunning Duke do anything she desires! Amazing girl!<br /><br />One aspect of this story I really liked was the fact that every character loved Léonie, and everybody was always ready to help and protect her. Among these, my favourite was Lord Rupert Alastair. He is fun, charming and I believe he could have been a perfect hero, too. Besides, he is the protagonist of one of my favourite scenes. I cannot and will not reveal any details but I can tell three things: Rupert, a stolen horse and an adventurous chase!<br /><br />Therefore, if you would like to meet His Grace the Duke of Avon and live with him, his friends and his enemies one of the most engaging experiences, you simply must grab a copy of “These old shades” and read it immediately. It is definitely a page-turner I highly recommend!<br /><br />Rating: 4.5 out of 5 stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="322855243040757410">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_129250132">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/129250132" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="left imgcol" title="Jane Stewart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" alt="Jane Stewart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/129250132?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 04, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="user" title="Jane Stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6781119-these-old-shades" title="Audiobook 9780754094777" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=historical-romance-prior-to-wwll" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance-prior-to-wwll</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=female-disguised-as-male" class="actionLinkLite">female-disguised-as-male</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=5-star-historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">5-star-historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer129250132">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11261075600947644047">A delight from the beginning. I was smiling a lot during the book. Wonderful storytelling.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />Characters are so entertaining. The way Justin speaks and the things he says are so funny to me. One of his oddities is calling his younger brother Rupert (an adult) and his ward (19) “my infants.” Rupert has some hilarious action and comments. For example, someone is kidnapped, and Rupert follows on foot chasing the horse drawn vehicle. He then continues following the kidnappers doing od</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11261075600947644047">A delight from the beginning. I was smiling a lot during the book. Wonderful storytelling.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />Characters are so entertaining. The way Justin speaks and the things he says are so funny to me. One of his oddities is calling his younger brother Rupert (an adult) and his ward (19) “my infants.” Rupert has some hilarious action and comments. For example, someone is kidnapped, and Rupert follows on foot chasing the horse drawn vehicle. He then continues following the kidnappers doing odd things. I laughed at how Rupert was so excited and saw this as an adventure. He thought this was great fun – even as he was getting shot. I’ve read many novels that included kidnapping, but I’ve never read one where the victim’s friend saw it as fun. This is an example of why the writing is different with the unexpected.<br /><br />As I was listening to a conversation between the Comte and his wife toward the end of the book, I thought how well done to see their motivations and feelings through dialogue, rather than having the author “tell” us. <br /><br />Although I knew it was a possibility, I didn’t expect the ending. It almost seemed odd, but yes it was a happy ending.<br /><br />I listened to the audiobook version. The narrator did a wonderful job “acting” the parts of the various characters. This is so much better than tv and movies. And it’s 11 hours of entertainment. There are different narrators. I listened to the one by Cornelius Garrett.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />The Comte needed a son so he could keep the family estate. The Comte’s wife delivers their only child, a girl. The Comte switches the baby with a local farmer’s baby boy. He pays the farmer to move away and raise the girl Leonie as his own. Twelve years later the farmer and his wife die. Their son Jean moves to Paris and opens a tavern. He takes Leonie with him and makes her dress as a boy. As a boy she is called Leon. Leon is beaten and mistreated during that time. One night as she is running from Jean, she bumps into Justin. Justin is intrigued with her appearance. He buys her from Jean to be his page. This is where the story begins. Leon continues dressing as a boy. Later Justin has her dressing as a girl and learning society manners. Then he introduces her to society. Justin has a motive beneath all this. He has hated the Comte for twenty years and plans revenge.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook length: 11 hours. Narrator: Cornelius Garrett. Swearing language: none. Sexual content: none. Setting: 1756 France and England. Published: 1926. Genre: historical romance, female disguised as male.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_655864120">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/655864120" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19300349-susan" class="left imgcol" title="Susan"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Susan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/655864120?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 01, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19300349-susan" class="user" title="Susan">Susan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311182.These_Old_Shades" title="Paperback 9780099465829" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer655864120">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11416786499565307548">I am sad to say that for me, this was not an enjoyable read. Fortunately, this was not my first Georgette Heyer and I would say do not judge the author by this book - the others I have read, Arabella, Frederica and Venetia were all books I loved and anticipate re-reading many times. Very Jane Austeneque, but with a wicked sense of wry humour. <br /><br />I liked the secondary characters in These Old Shades much better than the primary characters of the Duke of Avon and Léon/Léonie. It may be that I just pre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11416786499565307548">I am sad to say that for me, this was not an enjoyable read. Fortunately, this was not my first Georgette Heyer and I would say do not judge the author by this book - the others I have read, Arabella, Frederica and Venetia were all books I loved and anticipate re-reading many times. Very Jane Austeneque, but with a wicked sense of wry humour. <br /><br />I liked the secondary characters in These Old Shades much better than the primary characters of the Duke of Avon and Léon/Léonie. It may be that I just prefer the Regency era. I did not enjoy the language (all the "my dears"), but mainly, my lack of enjoyment stemmed from the fact that the 2 main characters were not appealing to me. I found the Duke too foppish (his white hands, his attire) and Léonie despite her impudence, was too subservient in how she interacted with the Duke. And all the "my infant", "my child" references were a) way too frequent and b) kind of creepy. I could only get through it with a stuggle and had to keep pretending those were terms of endearment (I kept imagining them in French rather than English). The narrative and descriptive passages were very much along the lines of other Heyer works I have enjoyed. The dialogue and main characters in this one were a real struggle.<br /><br />My recommendation...skip this one, she has written much better.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11416786499565307548">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical romance</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8795277">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2082489694968903664">I have read just about every Georgette Heyer book there is and have loved every one of them. She writes two types of genre - historical romance and mystery books. These are old-fashioned relationship/mystery books, written true to the language and customs of their day. Well written, great research - real page turners, every one of them.<br /><br />"These Old Shades" is one of my particular favorites. It has a very clever plot and dynamic, engaging, even sometimes wonderfully irritating characters (I have ye</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2082489694968903664">I have read just about every Georgette Heyer book there is and have loved every one of them. She writes two types of genre - historical romance and mystery books. These are old-fashioned relationship/mystery books, written true to the language and customs of their day. Well written, great research - real page turners, every one of them.<br /><br />"These Old Shades" is one of my particular favorites. It has a very clever plot and dynamic, engaging, even sometimes wonderfully irritating characters (I have yet to read a Heyer character who is not dynamic though). It's sequal is "The Devil's Cub."<br /><br />If you like Jane Austen at all, you will love Georgette Heyer.</span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10981127500744293847">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10981127500744293847">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10981127500744293847">...more</a>

    </div>
